### Round 1 | planner | planner_initial

- diagnosis: Task: infer the most likely AIE mechanism class (ICT, TICT, ESIPT, neutral aromatic, unknown) for the given molecule. Using the prepared shared structure (ready; C58H40N2S; 101 atoms; 10 rotatable bonds; high planarity/compactness proxies but still multiple torsional DOFs), the current top1 working hypothesis is TICT because the scaffold is a large, highly conjugated multi-phenyl/aryl-vinyl system where solution-phase twisting can open nonradiative channels and aggregation can restrict these motions (RIM/TICT-like). The top2 runner-up is neutral aromatic because the molecule is mostly polyaromatic with limited hetero atoms, so AIE may be dominated by generic restriction of intramolecular motions rather than a bona fide charge-transfer/twisted-charge-transfer state. Top1 is uncertain because (i) planarity proxy is high (may indicate less twisting than typical TICT dyes), (ii) donor–acceptor separation is not obvious, and (iii) without excited-state character (transition density, dipole change, solvatochromism) we cannot distinguish ‘TICT/ICT-driven’ from ‘neutral aromatic RIM’. Evidence that can separate top1 vs top2 later: low-cost excited-state calculations (S1 vertical excitation, oscillator strength, excited-state dipole/CT metrics) and/or torsion-scan snapshots indicating whether twisting strongly stabilizes S1 and reduces f; experimentally, strong solvatochromic shifts would support ICT/TICT over neutral aromatic. Macro can provide structure-level mechanistic priors from motifs (rotors, conjugation, hetero pattern) but cannot confirm excited-state CT. Microscopic (bounded) can compute a small set of vertical excitations and basic CT/dipole indicators to discriminate TICT/ICT vs neutral aromatic without expensive exhaustive optimization. First round should gather both macro priors and a minimal microscopic excitation/CT signature to reduce ambiguity early.

- action: macro_and_microscopic

- confidence: 0.45

- task_instruction: Run a first-round combined assessment: (1) Macro: motif-based mechanism triage emphasizing rotor count, conjugation, and presence/absence of ESIPT/strong D-A features; (2) Microscopic: low-cost bounded Amesp/aTB S0 optimization on the provided prepared structure and a small S1 vertical excitation set with basic CT indicators (excited-state dipole change / transition density localization if available).

- task_completion: Task was completed only in a capability-limited contracted form. - reasoning_summary: From the shared structure context, the molecule is a large neutral, rotor-rich poly(aromatic/aryl-vinylene) system with a small heteroaromatic unit (nsnc) and many phenyl rings. Topology indicates multiple potential twisting junctions (rotatable bonds = 10; torsion candidates = 10; branch points = 18) that could enable donor–acceptor decoupling required for TICT. However, the provided geometry proxies strongly indicate an overall extended and near-planar conformer in the selected structure (planarity_proxy ~0.97; compactness_proxy ~0.95; principal_span_proxy ~156), which is more consistent with a largely conjugated/planar neutral aromatic emitter unless specific donor–acceptor torsions are able to access orthogonal CT configurations in excited state. The donor/acceptor partition proxy (~0.5) suggests only moderate D–A separation (and hetero atom count is low, 3), so purely from macro structure the evidence for strong intramolecular CT driving TICT is mixed: torsional degrees of freedom exist, but the scaffold appears predominantly polyaromatic and geometrically planar/extended in the prepared conformer.
Capability limit note: This macro pass cannot compute excited-state charge-transfer metrics, torsion energy profiles, solvent effects, or packing/aggregate restrictions; it can only summarize deterministic topology and the provided geometry proxies from the prepared single-molecule conformer set.

- execution_plan: Use deterministic_macro_structure_scan to execute the bounded macro workflow with focus areas: Rotor-rich topology (rotatable bonds, torsion candidates, branch points) as prerequisite for twisting, Extent of aromaticity/conjugated scaffold (aromatic ring count, ring systems) vs localized D–A motif (heteroaromatic unit, hetero atom count), Geometry proxies indicating planarity/extension (planarity_proxy, principal_span_proxy) that may counter a ground-state twisted architecture, Neutrality/charge state as a coarse proxy for CT propensity (charge = 0). Planned local steps: [shared_context_load] Load the shared prepared structure context and reuse its descriptors. [focus_selection] Select the macro structural focus areas requested by the Planner instruction. [topology_analysis] Summarize rotor topology, ring systems, conjugation, and donor-acceptor layout. However, TICT remains plausible because the topology is rotor-rich (10 rotatable bonds; 10 torsion candidates; 18 branch points) and TICT is an excited-state relaxation phenomenon that may not appear at the single-conformer vertical-excitation baseline. Key remaining discriminator between neutral aromatic vs TICT is whether twisting around specific aryl–vinyl/biaryl junctions produces a lower-lying CT-like excited state (often with reduced oscillator strength and increased charge separation) relative to the near-planar bright state. No internal pairwise discriminative task has yet been completed for the current pair (neutral aromatic vs TICT). The best next action is therefore a bounded internal pairwise discriminative microscopic task that probes torsion dependence of the lowest excited states on a small set of key dihedrals.

However, the provided geometry proxies strongly indicate an overall extended and near-planar conformer in the selected structure (planarity_proxy ~0.97; compactness_proxy ~0.95; principal_span_proxy ~156), which is more consistent with a largely conjugated/planar neutral aromatic emitter unless specific donor–acceptor torsions are able to access orthogonal CT configurations in excited state. The donor/acceptor partition proxy (~0.5) suggests only moderate D–A separation (and hetero atom count is low, 3), so purely from macro structure the evidence for strong intramolecular CT driving TICT is mixed: torsional degrees of freedom exist, but the scaffold appears predominantly polyaromatic and geometrically planar/extended in the prepared conformer.

Internal pairwise discriminative task for this pair has already been completed (decisive).
